{"nick":"joepie91","message":"vladoski: think of the event loop as a big array of \"callbacks I need to call on the next iteration of a while(true) loop\"","date":"2019-05-07T14:48:08.109Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"plus an array of \"stuff I need to check, that might put a callback in that array\"","date":"2019-05-07T14:48:22.682Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(this is a bit simplified)","date":"2019-05-07T14:48:33.305Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"it just perpetually loops; reads the callback queue, executes each callback; looks at stuff that needs to be checked (\"has this timer been reached yet?\"), puts potentially new stuff in the callback queue","date":"2019-05-07T14:49:02.628Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"ad infinitum","date":"2019-05-07T14:49:04.310Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"the program ends when there are no callbacks and checks left to process, as that means that no code will ever run that will create new callbacks either","date":"2019-05-07T14:49:21.610Z","type":"message"}

{"nick":"joepie91","message":"xuib: there's no single answer to that; the short answer is \"both yes and no\", the longer answer is: 'packages' are basically just expressions that define how to build a particular 'package' from its source, each expression evaluates to a unique deterministic hash that represents that exact build configuration (and that changes when you do eg. overrides with additional patches), and there's transparent 'binary caching' in the form of Nix","date":"2019-05-07T21:45:40.735Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"automatically looking up each hash on your configured binary cache servers first, and only doing the build locally if the binary cache server doesn't have it","date":"2019-05-07T21:45:42.268Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(or if you have binary caches turned off, of course)","date":"2019-05-07T21:45:46.338Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"wiak","date":"2019-05-07T21:45:54.739Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"if the binary cache *does* have a pre-existing build for the hash (ie. build configuration) in question, it just downloads and unpacks that","date":"2019-05-07T21:46:18.012Z","type":"message"}
